Sanders Introduces PatriotCare, calling it universal patriotic healthcare for all.

Okay, so imagine this. Its like nationalism, except we give people healthcare instead of bombs. Wouldnt that be nice? -Bernie Sanders

The Jacksonist-allied House has passed a new bill in alignment with President Bernie Sanders domestic policy called PatriotCare. With the bill being passed, PatriotCare now proceeds to the Senate, where the Jacksonists hold a more stable majority, but may face greater challenges from within their own caucus. Web Archive: Moralnet

Free Internet > Regional Intranets > Alphanet (USA) > Moralnet > Category: Cultural Issues > Topic: Transhumanism

GodzillaKaiju2024: Human genetic modification violates the divinely ordained order of creation by presuming authority over human nature that belongs solely to God. Genesis 1:26-27. Let us make man in our image, after our likeness.

The Imago Dei is understood as the unique identity, dignity, and integrity of human beings as created by God. To re-engineer this nature, particularly at the level of DNA, which encodes the blueprint of life is tampering with the imago Dei itself. Therefore, it is against the divine order to tamper with it.

Genesis 1:28, fill the earth and subdue it. gives humans dominion over creation, but not over themselves as creatures. Dominion is stewardship, not sovereignty. Job 38:4: Where were you when I laid the foundation of the earth? God rebukes human presumption in claiming creative authority. Deuteronomy 29:29: The secret things belong to the Lord our God. This means that certain realms of creation, particularly those involving the essence of life, are divinely reserved and not for human mastery.

CodFisher: I disagree. These quotes, while strong on the surface, represent an unfortunately misunderstanding of what they entail. Lets go over them one by one. Genesis 1:26-27, the Imago Dei. I agree that God created man in his image, but disagree on what that entails. God does not have a physical body, there is no physical image he could be modelling us after. Therefore, the Imago Dei is better understood as humanitys capacity for knowledge, creativity, and rational thought. While Gods image isnt physical, the body still participates in that image as the vessel through which intellect and creativity manifest. Thus, modifying it responsibly can be a way of exercising, not erasing, the image of God. And while some radical transhumanists advocate for the restructuring of the human psychological structure, that is not what I am advocating for.

Genesis 1:28, while this does not give us sovereignty over ourselves, it does not say that we are not to alter ourselves whatsoever. A better verse for that is likely 1 Corinthians 6:19-20, our bodies are a temple of the Holy Spirit. But even this is taken out of context, as it is mentioned in the context of sexual immorality. If our bodies are temples, caring for them; strengthening, healing, even improving them through knowledge can be a form of reverence, not defilement. And in general, the pattern we see across the New Testament is that it is our thoughts and intentions, not actions, that matter most. 1 Samuel 16:7: People look at the outward appearance, but the LORD looks at the heart. Mark 7:15: Its not what goes into your body that defiles you; you are defiled by what comes from your heart.

Finally, Deuteronomy 29:29 does not forbid anything, only vaguely suggesting that there are secret and known worlds. It cannot be used as an argument against transhumanism unless you have already previously proved that transhumanism is part of this hidden world. We should respect the mystery of creation, but Scripture doesnt equate mystery with prohibition. Gods secrets remain his, but discovery has always been part of humanitys faithful response to curiosity.

As for my counter-argument, the Bible does not dictate any technology as being forbidden in of itself. Christ never condemned the advances of new technology made between the Old Testament and the New, nor did he advocate for returning to a more primitive lifestyle. The burden of proof that God is against technology ultimately falls on the arguer. Humans are creative creatures, creation is part of our design, and our call to partake in Gods creation. I find it unlikely that God would either not know about humanitys creative impulses, or that he did know, and choose to not speak out against it.

When technology has gone awry, most notably in the Tower of Babel, it is always the intent, and not the technology that is condemned. God is not opposed to building tall buildings, nor brick-laying, but instead the pride and hubris of man. In every major disaster, from the Flood, to Sodom and Gommorha, and more, it was always the heart of Man that ultimately invoked Gods wrath.

Finally, 1 Corinthians 15. The Bible talks about a spiritual glorified body. Now Im not saying that transhumanism will lead us to the glorified bodies they speak of. But this does show that ultimately, the physical bodies are not something sacred, as they will be replaced by better spiritual bodies.

Ultimately, it is the intent, and not the technology itself to be condemned. The bigger danger is not that we invent transhumanism at all, but that it distracts us from God, and becomes another technological idol, a golden calf. But this does not mean we should turn away from the technology. Weve had this exact same idolatry scare with every new technology weve invented. From machines, to computers, to artificial intelligence. But each time, weve been able to remember our creations are not God, the church adapts, and we continue forward.

On Elections

In the aftermath of Williams reforms, the transition from electoral college to popular vote, the nature of American elections were changed forever. Now, rather than the states, the people themselves voted. Turnout increased, as elections became races to see who could get the most votes, regardless of where they were. The swing states, as they were once called, lost prominence, as campaigns became focused on population centers.

Anti-Utopia

A Parable of the Postmodern World by Richard wong

Published 2106

#6 in Heterodox Moralist Literature

Description:

One mans utopia is anothers dystopia. But why? Perhaps it is because they are the same thing, born from the false idea that humanity is a system to be optimized.

Anti-Utopia is a work that warns against the utopian paradigm of modern man. In a time when the Moralist movement seems more fanatical and utopian than ever, the call comes from inside the house, as Richard Wong warns that utopianism without humility, without humanity is but ruin of the soul.

The book takes place in the year 3000, after the collapse of the Utopia Project, and follows the work of the Moral, a governing body learning from the mistakes of their predecessors, continuing in mans never-ending quest to find peace in this life. What does it mean to be human? What does it mean to create utopia? And what is the ultimate goal of human existence?

Average Rating: 3.6 Stars out of 5.

Recent Reviews:

Good ideas, mixed writing. (4/5)

Theres something deeply frustrating yet charming about this writing. It really does read like a modern parable, with the flowery, poetic language. It sounds like something the village elder would tell you over a campfire.

But the writing seems to be way too focused on the world itself and not the many half baked characters Wong seems to come up with and toss away. But the ideas are genuinely interesting enough, and the world Wong comes up with is one that is worth dreaming about.

Libertarian wish fulfillment (3/5)

Im not going to spend any effort on the characters or plot, since its obvious Wong didnt either. This is less of a book and more of a utopian wish fantasy about the society Wong wishes to see. His basic ideas boil down to:

One, utopianism treats humans as machines to be optimized, leading to suffering as humans cannot be tuned like a machine.

Two, the optimal form of government is one which allows humanity to flourish on its own terms within a safe controlled environment. He generally believes human happiness to be outside the purview of government, and the governments job is to leave the people to pursue their own happiness, while providing the stability needed to ensure this environment.

The ideas are almost libertarian in nature, honestly surprising coming from a self-proclaimed Christian Moralist, but what do I know? Basically, treat this book like you would something like Atlas Shrugged. 70% ideological wish fulfillment, 30% rushed plot.`, "drowning": `
